            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Nanotechnol. has opened up new frontiers in materials science and engineering in the past several decades.  Considerable efforts on nanostructured electrode materials have been made in recent years to fulfill the future requirements of electrochem. energy storage.  Compared to bulk materials, most of these nanostructured electrode materials improve the thermodn. and kinetic properties of electrochem. reactions for achieving high energy and power densities.  Here we briefly review the state-of-the-art research activities in the area of nanostructured pos. electrode materials for post-lithium ion batteries, including Li-S batteries, Li-Se batteries, aq. rechargeable lithium batteries, Li-O2 batteries, Na-ion batteries, Mg-ion batteries and Al-ion batteries.  These future rechargeable battery systems may offer increased energy densities, reduced cost, and more environmental benignity.  A particular focus is directed to the design principles of these nanostructured pos. electrode materials and how nanostructuring influences electrochem. performance.  Moreover, the recent achievements in nanostructured pos. electrode materials for some of the latest emerging rechargeable batteries are also summarized, such as Zn-ion batteries, F- and Cl-ion batteries, Na-, K- and Al-S batteries, Na- and K-O2 batteries, Li-CO2 batteries, novel Zn-air batteries, and hybrid redox flow batteries.  To facilitate further research and development, some future research trends and directions are finally discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9_eyoH8Ij6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Gd7pb_X0Ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFKjtr3E&amp;md5=4875475022bc8842c68bc83b761e177c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201800028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cuniberti, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Dual-Stimuli-Responsive Sodium-Bromine Battery with Ultrahigh Energy Density</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molecular Cooperative Assembly-Mediated Synthesis of Ultra-High-Performance Hard Carbon Anodes for Dual-Carbon Sodium Hybrid Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Hui-Ju; Huh, Yun Suk; Im, Won Bin; Jun, Young-Si</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11935-11946</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although sodium hybrid capacitors (NHCs) have emerged as one of the most promising next-generation energy storage systems, further advancement is delayed primarily by the absence of high-performance battery-type anodes.  Herein, we report a nature-inspired synthesis route to prep. hard carbon anodes with high capacity, rate capability, and cycle stability for dual-carbon NHCs.  Shape- and size-controllable crystal aggregates of inexpensive triazine mols. are utilized as reactive templates that perform triple duties of structure-directing agent, porogen, and nitrogen source.  This enables the fine control of microstructure/morphol./compn. and thereby electrochem. reactions toward Na-ion.  The resulting hard carbon optimized in terms of lateral size, interlayer spacing, and surface affinity of graphene-like layers achieves a specific capacity of ∼380 mAh/g after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 250 mA/g mainly via intercalation, the current record of hard carbons.  Combined with a com. microporous carbon fiber cathode, the full cell is able to deliver a volumetric energy d. of 2.89 mWh/cm3 and a volumetric power d. of 160 mW/cm3, outperforming NHCs based on inorg. Na-ion anode materials.  More importantly, such performance could not only be retained for 10000 cycles (4.5 F/cm3 at 10 mA/cm3) with 0.000 028 6% loss per cycle at &gt;97% Coulombic efficiency but also successfully transferred to flexible pouch cells without significant performance loss after 300 bending cycles or during wrapping at a 10R condition.  Simple prepn. of hard carbon anodes using org. crystal reactive templates, therefore, demonstrates great potential for the manuf. of high-performance flexible NHCs using only carbon electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrr43XdcRZRfbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Gd7pb_X0Ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFSisr3J&amp;md5=846f3cecc2fa18d99b7f9dd0540f08c5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201802800"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tervoort, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oschatz, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Antonietti, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niederberger, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast Na-Ion Intercalation in Zinc Vanadate for High-Performance Na-Ion Hybrid Capacitor</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Materials for Sodium-Ion Capacitors with Superior Energy-Power Properties: Progress and Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hongwei; Hu, Mingxiang; Lv, Qian; Huang, Zheng-Hong; Kang, Feiyu; Lv, Ruitao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing electrochem. energy storage devices with high energy-power densities, long cycling life, as well as low cost is of great significance.  Sodium-ion capacitors (NICs), with Na+ as carriers, are composed of a high capacity battery-type electrode and a high rate capacitive electrode.  However, unlike their lithium-ion analogs, the research on NICs is still in its infancy.  Rational material designs still need to be developed to meet the increasing requirements for NICs with superior energy-power performance and low cost.  In the past few years, various materials have been explored to develop NICs with the merits of superior electrochem. performance, low cost, good stability, and environmental friendliness.  Here, the material design strategies for sodium-ion capacitors are summarized, with focus on cathode materials, anode materials, and electrolytes.  The challenges and opportunities ahead for the future research on materials for NICs are also proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDLk9bvcz3w7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Gd7pb_X0Ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVCmsLfM&amp;md5=7be1522fec67c8ece2880323bb2a21b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201802272"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paek, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Direct Structure-Performance Comparison of All-Carbon Potassium and Sodium Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct Structure-Performance Comparison of All-Carbon Potassium and Sodium Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Ziqiang; Wu Mengqiang; Chen Zhi; Chen Cheng; Yang Jian; Feng Tingting; Paek Eunsu; Mitlin David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1802272</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A hybrid ion capacitor (HIC) based on potassium ions (K(+)) is a new high-power intermediate energy device that may occupy a unique position on the Ragone chart space.  Here, a direct performance comparison of a potassium ion capacitor (KIC) versus the better-known sodium ion capacitor is provided.  Tests are performed with an asymmetric architecture based on bulk ion insertion, partially ordered, dense carbon anode (hard carbon, HC) opposing N- and O-rich ion adsorption, high surface area, cathode (activated carbon, AC).  A classical symmetric "supercapacitor-like" configuration AC-AC is analyzed in parallel.  For asymmetric K-based HC-AC devices, there are significant high-rate limitations associated with ion insertion into the anode, making it much inferior to Na-based HC-AC devices.  A much larger charge-discharge hysteresis (overpotential), more than an order of magnitude higher impedance RSEI, and much worse cyclability are observed.  However, K-based AC-AC devices obtained on-par energy, power, and cyclability with their Na counterpart.  Therefore, while KICs are extremely scientifically interesting, more work is needed to tailor the structure of  "Na-inherited" dense carbon anodes and electrolytes for satisfactory K ion insertion.  Conversely, it should be possible to utilize many existing high surface area adsorption carbons for fast rate K application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGccaQRmYaT1Zoq0fPSOTvfW6udTcc2eYt-q9YD0Inirntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3MvkslGguw%253D%253D&amp;md5=3f6dbd19dcbb49876486c776bec9f73a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201903895"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Au, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tebyetekerwa, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">All-Cellulose-Based Quasi-Solid-State Sodium-Ion Hybrid Capacitors Enabled by Structural Hierarchy</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The general construction of asymmetric bowl-like hollow nanostructures by grafting carbon-sheathed ultrasmall iron-based compounds onto carbon surfaces for use as superior anodes for sodium-ion hybrid capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Jingyu; Li, Yapeng; Peng, Bo; Wang, Gongrui; Zhang, Genqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24199-24204</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lack of appropriate anode candidates displaying ultrafast sodium insertion/extn. capabilities to match the capacitive behavior of cathodes has become a very challenging issue.  In the current work, we developed a feasible yet general strategy to construct novel bowl-like hollow particles with dual-carbon protection consisting of ultrasmall iron-based-compd. nanodots embedded into a carbon matrix (denoted as C@FeX, X = O/S/Se/P).  The bowl-like C@Fe-X exhibited superior sodium ion storage, in particular high specific capacity and excellent cycling stability and rate capabilities, when evaluated as an anode.  Specifically, the bowl-like hollow C@FeSe2 particles delivered excellent cycling stability with negligible fading of capacity under a high rate of 20 A g-1 for 6000 cycles, and maintained 42.0% of the initial specific capacity with the c.d. ranging from 0.1 to 20 A g-1.  More importantly, the NIHCs based on the anode made of the bowl-like C@FeP particles showed a high energy d. of 133.6 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 200 W kg-1, demonstrating great potential for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoU3fbEEsE-xLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeTZw1sVgn_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFWit7zJ&amp;md5=d0388c6dccf5c90d1240101a09dc57b2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201902858"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Josef, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Leus, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niederberger, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hofmann, J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Printing of Porous Nitrogen-Doped Ti3C2 MXene Scaffolds for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Hybrid Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan Zhaodi; Wei Chaohui; Yu Lianghao; Xia Zhou; Cai Jingsheng; Tian Zhengnan; Zou Guifu; Sun Jingyu; Xia Zhou; Sun Jingyu; Dou Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">867-876</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">3D printing technology has stimulated a burgeoning interest to fabricate customized architectures in a facile and scalable manner targeting wide ranged energy storage applications.  Nevertheless, 3D-printed hybrid capacitor devices synergizing favorable energy/power density have not yet been explored thus far.  Herein, we demonstrate a 3D-printed sodium-ion hybrid capacitor (SIC) based on nitrogen-doped MXene (N-Ti3C2Tx) anode and activated carbon cathode.  N-Ti3C2Tx affording a well-defined porous structure and uniform nitrogen doping can be obtained via a sacrificial template method.  Thus-formulated ink can be directly printed to form electrode architecture without the request of a conventional current collector.  The 3D-printed SICs, with a large areal mass loading up to 15.2 mg cm(-2), can harvest an areal energy/power density of 1.18 mWh cm(-2)/40.15 mW cm(-2), outperforming the state-of-the-art 3D-printed energy storage devices.  Furthermore, our SIC also achieves a gravimetric energy/power density of 101.6 Wh kg(-1)/3269 W kg(-1).  This work demonstrates that the 3D printing technology is versatile enough to construct emerging energy storage systems reconciling high energy and power density.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSRf7C7Sx3Zx4NpW7w2tapOfW6udTcc2eaZqG05UeTs0rntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3Mbmt1Cjsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=cab9c607cbcf0b3d6ddac97c4b1f204a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.07.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chojnacka, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jėowski, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Béguin, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Performance Hybrid Sodium-Ion Capacitor with Tin Phosphide used as Battery-Type Negative Electrode</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">200</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">206</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">All-Solid-State Planar Sodium-Ion Microcapacitors with Multidirectional Fast Ion Diffusion Pathways</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Shuanghao; Wang, Sen; Dong, Yanfeng; Zhou, Feng; Qin, Jieqiong; Wang, Xiao; Su, Feng; Sun, Chenglin; Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Cheng, Hui-Ming; Bao, Xinhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1902147</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the relentless development of smart and miniaturized electronics, the worldwide thirst for microscale electrochem. energy storage devices with form factors is launching a new era of competition.  Herein, the first prototype planar sodium-ion microcapacitors are constructed based on the interdigital microelectrodes of urchin-like sodium titanate as faradaic anode and nanoporous activated graphene as non-faradaic cathode along with high-voltage ionogel electrolyte on a single flexible substrate.  By effectively coupling with battery-type anode and capacitor-type cathode, the resultant all-solid-state NIMCs working at 3.5 V exhibit a high volumetric energy d. of 37.1 mWh cm-3 and an ultralow self-discharge rate of 44 h from Vmax to 0.6 Vmax, both of which surpass most reported hybrid micro-supercapacitors.  Through tuning graphene layer covered on the top surface of interdigital microelectrodes, the NIMCs unveil remarkably enhanced power d., owing to the establishment of favorable multidirectional fast ion diffusion pathways that significantly reduce the charge transfer resistance.  Meanwhile, the as-fabricated NIMCs present excellent mech. flexibility without capacitance fade under repeated deformation, and electrochem. stability at a high temp. of 80 °C because of using nonflammable ionogel electrolyte and in-plane geometry.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLytkg5c6aP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeTZw1sVgn_A"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous nitrogen-doped carbon/carbon nanocomposite electrodes enable sodium ion capacitors with high capacity and rate capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Runyu; Leus, Karen; Hofmann, Jan P.; Antonietti, Markus; Oschatz, Martin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">67</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104240</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The realization of electrochem. energy storage devices combining high energy and power d. places high demands on the electrode materials.  It remains difficult to provide high metal storage capacity and rate capability at the same time in one and the same material.  By decoupling metal storage and electron transport in different phases of a nanostructured electrode composed of nitrogen-rich carbon nanoparticles which are embedded into a conductive mesoporous carbon matrix, this dilemma can be minimized.  The composite material has a remarkable performance for sodium storage with a reversible capacity of 343 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and capacity retention of 124 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1.  This work shows that a properly designed nanocomposite material can fulfill both requirements and sheds new light on resolving the seemingly conflicting energy/power d. demands in current electrochem. energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOQNiUCWVdsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzrlS0u_P_TQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFOlt7%252FP&amp;md5=4d92c1ae5c8fd049a7da0496511042a5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.152732"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uniform Yolk–Shell Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>@C Nanoboxes as a General Host Material for the Efficient Storage of Alkali Metal Ions</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform yolk-shell Fe7S8@C nanoboxes as a general host material for the efficient storage of alkali metal ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Weng, Wangsuo; Xu, Jingyi; Lai, Chenling; Xu, Zhenhua; Du, Yichen; Lin, Jun; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">817</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">152732</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe sulfides are potential anode materials for the reversible electrochem. storage of alkali metal ions (Li+, Na+, or K+) from the perspective of high theor. capacity and relatively low cost.  Nevertheless, their real application is greatly hampered by the inferior cond. and the huge vol. variations in the reaction with alkali metal ions.  Few studies have examd. desirable candidates that can be used as current host materials for alkali metal ions.  A mild etching approach coupled with further sulfidation is proposed for the precise design and prepn. of uniform yolk-shell Fe7S8@C nanoboxes.  The as-prepd. yolk-shell Fe7S8@C nanoboxes exhibit excellent storage performance for alkali metal ions in the aspects of high specific capacity, superior cyclic stability, and good rate performance. Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability.  With the same themes in mind, the authors also highlight current and future electrochem. storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion battery is a potential sustainable energy storage system due to its abundance and low cost.  To date, some Na-storage anode materials have achieved long life span, but the rate performance still remains insufficient.  Herein, in some linear ether-based electrolytes, graphite can not only render unprecedented cyclability (∼6000 cycles), but also exhibit ultrahigh rate capability (up to 10 A g-1), along with a reversible capacity of ∼110 mAh g-1. (e.g. in situ Raman and ex situ XRD measurements), the authors reveal that graphite undergoes a stage-evolution mechanism induced by the insertion of solvated Na ions.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljA2sYMRIXz-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-10551-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tailoring sodium intercalation in graphite for high energy and power sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Zheng-Long; Yoon Gabin; Park Kyu-Young; Park Hyeokjun; Tamwattana Orapa; Joo Kim Sung; Seong Won Mo; Kang Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2598</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Co-intercalation reactions make graphite as promising anodes for sodium ion batteries, however, the high redox potentials significantly lower the energy density.  Herein, we investigate the factors that influence the co-intercalation potential of graphite and find that the tuning of the voltage as large as 0.38 V is achievable by adjusting the relative stability of ternary graphite intercalation compounds and the solvent activity in electrolytes.  The feasibility of graphite anode in sodium ion batteries is confirmed in conjunction with Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathodes by using the optimal electrolyte.  The sodium ion battery delivers an improved voltage of 3.1 V, a high power density of 3863 W kg(-1)both electrodes, negligible temperature dependency of energy/power densities and an extremely low capacity fading rate of 0.007% per cycle over 1000 cycles, which are among the best thus far reported for sodium ion full cells, making it a competitive choice in large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQjujM6HaRzJmZyxfu64m4ffW6udTcc2ebhLHCwq-8FxLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3M3msFGisw%253D%253D&amp;md5=0294b72b45bf5f4a18e760d720842e70</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE00546F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seidl, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bucher, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hartung, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Martens, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schneider, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stimming, U.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intercalation of Solvated Na-Ions into Graphite</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation of solvated Na-ions into graphite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Seidl, L.; Bucher, N.; Chu, E.; Hartung, S.; Martens, S.; Schneider, O.; Stimming, U.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1631-1642</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The reversible intercalation of solvated Na-ions into graphite and the concomitant formation of ternary Na-graphite intercalation compds. (GICs) are studied using several in operando techniques, such as X-ray-diffraction (XRD), electrochem. scanning tunnelling microscopy (EC-STM) and electrochem. quartz crystal microbalance techniques (EQCM).  Linear ethylene glycol di-Me ether homologues ("glymes") Gx with x + 1 O-atoms were used as solvents, where x is 1-4.  The intercalation mechanism of Na+(Gx)y-complexes was investigated with a focus on the phase transitions and diffusion rates of the Na+(Gx)y-complexes inside the graphite lattice.  For the four shortest glymes (G1 to G4), it is found using XRD that an intermediate stage 2 Na-GIC (NaC48) is formed upon the partial sodiation of the graphite electrode.  At full sodiation stage 1 Na-GIC (NaC18, 112 mA h g-1) is obtained for G1, G2 and G4, while the G3 system also forms a stage 1 Na-GIC but with less Na incorporated (NaC30, 70 mA h g-1).  The phase transitions of a battery electrode upon ion-intercalation are visualised using STM on the at. scale for the first time.  In addn., the local diffusion rates of the intercalated species inside the electrode were detd., a unique approach for detg. kinetic effects in batteries on the at. scale.  The formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is obsd. with STM as well as with an EQCM, while the latter technique is used for novel in situ hydrodynamic spectroscopy, giving further insight into the intercalation mechanism.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpHio6VJZG8HLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljA2sYMRIXz-g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Staging Na/K-ion de-/intercalation of graphite retrieved from spent Li-ion batteries: in operando X-ray diffraction studies and an advanced anode material for Na/K-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Hao-Jie; Hou, Bao-Hua; Li, Wen-Hao; Ning, Qiu-Li; Yang, Xu; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Nie, Xue-Jiao; Wang, Guang; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The graphite material from exhausted Li-ion batteries (LIBs) is reused as a favorable anode for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) and K-ion batteries (KIBs) through a recycling treatment.  The optimized electrode delivers improved electrochem. performance, such as 162 mA h g-1 in NIBs at 0.2 A g-1 and 320 mA h g-1 in KIBs at 0.05 A g-1.  In addn., the insights into Na/K-ion de-/intercalation model evolution and corresponding electrochem. anal. are conducted through in operando X-ray diffraction and a series of other characterization methods, discovering a visible transitional stage for NIBs and an irreversible initial cycle phase transformation for KIBs. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Origin of Excellent Rate and Cycle Performance of Na<sup>+</sup>-Solvent Cointercalated Graphite vs. Poor Performance of Li<sup>+</sup> -Solvent Case</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">456</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">462</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.03.015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D456-462%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DS.%2BC.%2BJung%26author%3DY.-J.%2BKang%26author%3DY.-K.%2BHan%26title%3DOrigin%2Bof%2BExcellent%2BRate%2Band%2BCycle%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BNa%252B-Solvent%2BCointercalated%2BGraphite%2Bvs.%2BPoor%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BLi%252B%2B-Solvent%2BCase%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.03.015&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c14611&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.03.015&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of excellent rate and cycle performance of Na+-solvent cointercalated graphite vs. poor performance of Li+-solvent case</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Sung Chul; Kang, Yong-Ju; Han, Young-Kyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">456-462</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite its high reversibility for Li+ intercalation, graphite is known to be electrochem. inactive for Na+ intercalation.  On the contrary, recent studies have demonstrated that graphite is active and shows excellent rate and cycle performance for Na+-solvent cointercalation but it exhibits poor performance for Li+-solvent cointercalation.  Herein, we elucidate the mechanism of Li+- and Na+-solvent cointercalation into graphite and the origin of the strikingly different electrochem. performance of Li+- and Na+-solvent cointercalation cells.  Na+ intercalation into graphite is thermodynamically unfavorable, but Na+-diglyme cointercalation is very favorable.  The diglyme-graphene van der Waals interaction reinforces the interlayer coupling strength and thereby improves the resistance of graphite to exfoliation.  The transport of solvated Na ions is so fast that the diffusivity of Na+-diglyme complexes is markedly faster (by five orders of magnitude) than that of Li+-diglyme complexes.  The very fast Na+-diglyme cond. is attributed to facile sliding of flat diglyme mols., which completely solvate Na ions in the interlayer space of graphite.  The slow Li+-diglyme cond. is ascribed to steric hindrance to codiffusion caused by bent diglyme mols. that incompletely solvate Li ions.  The bent and flat diglyme mols. surrounding Li and Na ions, resp., are highly assocd. with the strong Li+-graphene and weak Na+-graphene interactions, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIBciXioUE5LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNqEitnWBfw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktFygtbo%253D&amp;md5=9b106c4199d530c12545837c216bc169</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201801361"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ethers Illume Sodium-Based Battery Chemistry: Uniqueness, Surprise, and Challenges</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">370-376</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNqEitnWBfw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2mtbnN&amp;md5=be5958dc01f38deeacf6a2a0eb32101f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acscentsci.5b00328"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seh, Z.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Highly Reversible Room-Temperature Sodium Metal Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Seh, Zhi Wei; Sun, Jie; Sun, Yongming; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Central Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">449-455</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to its low cost and high natural abundance, sodium metal is among the most promising anode materials for energy storage technologies beyond lithium ion batteries.  However, room-temp. sodium metal anodes suffer from poor reversibility during long-term plating and stripping, mainly due to formation of nonuniform solid electrolyte interphase as well as dendritic growth of sodium metal.  Herein it is reported for the first time that a simple liq. electrolyte, sodium hexafluorophosphate in glymes (mono-, di-, and tetraglyme), can enable highly reversible and nondendritic plating-stripping of sodium metal anodes at room temp.  High av. Coulombic efficiencies of 99.9% were achieved over 300 plating-stripping cycles at 0.5 mA cm-2.  The long-term reversibility was found to arise from the formation of a uniform, inorg. solid electrolyte interphase made of sodium oxide and sodium fluoride, which is highly impermeable to electrolyte solvent and conducive to nondendritic growth.  As a proof of concept, a room-temp. sodium-sulfur battery is demonstrated using this class of electrolytes, paving the way for the development of next-generation, sodium-based energy storage technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdqXOWzEW74bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNqEitnWBfw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVGmtrfL&amp;md5=6155e3c781a24b8340081c2ad4444616</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/ja5017156"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parvez, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exfoliation of Graphite into Graphene in Aqueous Solutions of Inorganic Salts</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Parvez, Khaled; Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Li, Rongjin; Liu, Xianjie; Graf, Robert; Feng, Xinliang; Muellen, Klaus</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mass prodn. of high-quality graphene sheets is essential for their practical application in electronics, optoelectronics, composite materials, and energy-storage devices.  Here the authors report a prompt electrochem. exfoliation of graphene sheets into aq. solns. of different inorg. salts ((NH4)2SO4, Na2SO4, K2SO4, etc.).  Exfoliation in these electrolytes leads to graphene with a high yield (&gt;85%, ≤3 layers), large lateral size (up to 44 μm), low oxidn. degree (a C/O ratio of 17.2), and a remarkable hole mobility of 310 cm2 V-1 s-1.  Further, highly conductive graphene films (11 Ω sq-1) are readily fabricated on an A4-size paper by applying brush painting of a concd. graphene ink (10 mg mL-1, in N,N'-DMF).  All-solid-state flexible supercapacitors manufd. from such graphene films deliver a high area capacitance of 11.3 mF cm-2 and an excellent rate capability of 5000 mV s-1.  The described electrochem. exfoliation shows great promise for the industrial-scale synthesis of high-quality graphene for numerous advanced applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoPivpRxHMPqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNqEitnWBfw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXltFGmsbs%253D&amp;md5=d641761b307c6677524aefefeeca6de2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1524/zkri.220.5.567.65075"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Clark, S.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen vacancies enhance pseudocapacitive charge storage properties of MoO3-x</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyung-Seok; Cook, John B.; Lin, Hao; Ko, Jesse S.; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Ozolins, Vidvuds; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The short charging times and high power capabilities assocd. with capacitive energy storage make this approach an attractive alternative to batteries.  One limitation of electrochem. capacitors is their low energy d. and for this reason, there is widespread interest in pseudocapacitive materials that use Faradaic reactions to store charge.  One candidate pseudocapacitive material is orthorhombic MoO3 (α-MoO3), a layered compd. with a high theor. capacity for lithium (279 mA h g-1 or 1,005 C g-1).  Here, we report on the properties of reduced α-MoO3-x(R-MoO3-x) and compare it with fully oxidized α-MoO3 (F-MoO3).  The introduction of oxygen vacancies leads to a larger interlayer spacing that promotes faster charge storage kinetics and enables the α-MoO3 structure to be retained during the insertion and removal of Li ions.  The higher specific capacity of the R-MoO3-x is attributed to the reversible formation of a significant amt. of Mo4+ following lithiation.  This study underscores the potential importance of incorporating oxygen vacancies into transition metal oxides as a strategy for increasing the charge storage kinetics of redox-active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9QgRHEtnVrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-u0ZPT43ukA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fully Conjugated Phthalocyanine Copper Metal-Organic Frameworks for Sodium-Iodine Batteries with Long-Time-Cycling Durability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Faxing; Liu, Zaichun; Yang, Chongqing; Zhong, Haixia; Nam, Gyutae; Zhang, Panpan; Dong, Renhao; Wu, Yuping; Cho, Jaephil; Zhang, Jian; Feng, Xinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1905361</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-iodine (Na-I2) batteries are attracting growing attention for grid-scale energy storage due to their abundant resources, low cost, environmental friendliness, high theor. capacity (211 mAh g-1), and excellent electrochem. reversibility.  Nevertheless, the practical application of Na-I2 batteries is severely hindered by their poor cycle stability owing to the serious dissoln. of polyiodide in the electrolyte during charge/discharge processes.  Herein, the at. modulation of metal-bis(dihydroxy) species in a fully conjugated phthalocyanine copper metal-org. framework (MOF) for suppression of polyiodide dissoln. toward long-time cycling Na-I2 batteries is demonstrated.  The Fe2[(2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxy phthalocyaninato)Cu] MOF composited with I2 (Fe2-O8-PcCu/I2) serves as a cathode for a Na-I2 battery exhibiting a stable specific capacity of 150 mAh g-1 after 3200 cycles and outperforming the state-of-the-art cathodes for Na-I2 batteries.  Operando spectroelectrochem. and electrochem. kinetics analyses together with d. functional theory calcns. reveal that the square planar iron-bis(dihydroxy) (Fe-O4) species in Fe2-O8-PcCu are responsible for the binding of polyiodide to restrain its dissoln. into electrolyte.  Besides the monovalent Na-I2 batteries in org. electrolytes, the Fe2-O8-PcCu/I2 cathode also operates stably in other metal-I2 batteries like aq. multivalent Zn-I2 batteries.  Thus, this work offers a new strategy for designing stable cathode materials toward high-performance metal-iodine batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhvcsvJGd9v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVmsubicXS2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlGhsbzO&amp;md5=0d741d425306ce9906ec6dd05d3b31fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202000287"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tseng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Stimulus-Responsive Zinc-Iodine Battery with Smart Overcharge Self-Protection Function</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e2000287</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Stimulus-Responsive Zinc-Iodine Battery with Smart Overcharge Self-Protection Function</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Faxing; Tseng, Jochi; Liu, Zaichun; Zhang, Panpan; Wang, Gang; Chen, Guangbo; Wu, Weixing; Yu, Minghao; Wu, Yuping; Feng, Xinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000287</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Zinc-iodine aq. batteries (ZIABs) are highly attractive for grid-scale energy storage due to their high theor. capacities, environmental friendliness, and intrinsic non-flammability.  However, because of the close redox potential of Zn stripping/platting and hydrogen evolution, slight overcharge of ZIABs would induce drastic side reactions, serious safety concerns, and battery failure.  A novel type of stimulus-responsive zinc-iodine aq. battery (SR-ZIAB) with fast overcharge self-protection ability is demonstrated by employing a smart pH-responsive electrolyte.  Operando spectroelectrochem. characterizations reveal that the battery failure mechanism of ZIABs during overcharge arises from the increase of electrolyte pH induced by hydrogen evolution as well as the consequent irreversible formation of insulating ZnO at anode and sol. Zn(IO3)2 at cathode.  Under overcharge conditions, the designed SR-ZIABs can be rapidly switched off with capacity degrading to 6% of the initial capacity, thereby avoiding continuous battery damage.  Importantly, SR-ZIABs can be switched on with nearly 100% of capacity recovery by re-adjusting the electrolyte pH.  This work will inspire the development of aq. Zn batteries with smart self-protection ability in the overcharge state.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmkDQhzRAHrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVmsubicXS2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXksVKjsbc%253D&amp;md5=420bb5825ba13bcc6777faf3ae76eb57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.07.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, F.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design and Synthesis of Electrode Materials with Both Battery-Type and Capacitive Charge Storage</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">235</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">255</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Array of nanosheets render ultrafast and high-capacity Na-ion storage by tunable pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Yang, Peihua; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Wang, Jin; Fan, Xiaofeng; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Fan, Hong Jin; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a potentially low-cost and safe alternative to the prevailing lithium-ion battery technol.  However, it is a great challenge to achieve fast charging and high power d. for most sodium-ion electrodes because of the sluggish sodiation kinetics.  Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.  The graphene foam supported tin(II) sulfide nanoarray anode delivers a high reversible capacity of ∼1,100 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 and ∼420 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1, which even outperforms its lithium-ion storage performance.  The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVSw-KQ43s-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVmsubicXS2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFSqtLbO&amp;md5=3f7ab452279e7159794a832183e58387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/nl504764m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muller, G.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-layer and few-layer transition metal dichalcogenides have been extensively studied for their electronic properties, but their energy-storage potential has not been well explored.  This paper describes the structural and electrochem. properties of few-layer TiS2 nanocrystals.  The two-dimensional morphol. leads to very different behavior, compared to corresponding bulk materials.  Only small structural changes occur during lithiation/delithiation and charge storage characteristics are consistent with intercalation pseudocapacitance, leading to materials that exhibit both high energy and power d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrMEHWzqPoFmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVmsubicXS2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXit12msLg%253D&amp;md5=8a06a4dfc4a4da03e4c3cc5852b9c947</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b04610"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intercalation Pseudocapacitance in Ultrathin VOPO<sub>4</sub> Nanosheets: Toward High-Rate Alkali-Ion-Based Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">742</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">747</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation Pseudocapacitance in Ultrathin VOPO4 Nanosheets: Toward High-Rate Alkali-Ion-Based Electrochemical Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yue; Peng, Lele; Chen, Dahong; Yu, Guihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">742-747</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">There is a growing need for energy storage devices in numerous applications where a large amt. of energy needs to be either stored or delivered quickly.  The present paper details the study of alkali-ion intercalation pseudo-capacitance in ultrathin VOPO4 nanosheets, which hold promise in high-rate alkali-ion based electrochem. energy storage.  Starting from bulk VOPO4·2H2O chunks, VOPO4 nanosheets were obtained through simple ultrasonication in isoPrOH.  These nanosheets as the cathode exhibit a specific capacity of 154 and 136 mA h/g (close to theor. value 166 mA h/g) for Li and Na storage devices at 0.1 C and 100 and ∼70 mA h/g at 5 C, demonstrating their high rate capability.  Also, the capacity retention is maintained at 90% for Li ion storage and 73% for Na ion storage after 500 cycles, showing their reasonable stability.  The demonstrated alkali-ion intercalation pseudo-capacitance represents a promising direction for developing battery materials with promising high rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcpNKNsHXvp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVmsubicXS2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVejtb3F&amp;md5=1da7e7e855bb254dd6f51c674fbb8c11</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.03.186"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Opitz, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wallauer, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Smarsly, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Roling, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanisms of Charge Storage in Nanoparticulate TiO<sub>2</sub> and Li<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>5</sub>O<sub>12</sub> Anodes: New Insights from Scan Rate-Dependent Cyclic Voltammetry</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanisms of Charge Storage in Nanoparticulate TiO2 and Li4Ti5O12 Anodes: New Insights from Scan rate-dependent Cyclic Voltammetry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Opitz, Martin; Yue, Junpei; Wallauer, Jens; Smarsly, Bernd; Roling, Bernhard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors have studied Li intercalation into two nanoparticulate anode materials for Li ion batteries, Nb-doped TiO2 (Nb-TiO2) and Li4Ti5O12 (LTO), by scan rate-dependent cyclic voltammetry.  The av. particle size is 7 nm for Nb-TiO2 and 6 nm for LTO, resp.  For both materials, the authors observe a transition in the scan rate dependence of the charge flow, from Li intercalation capacity control at low scan rates to diffusion/phase transformation control at higher scan rates.  The peak current densities exhibit an approx. power law dependence on the scan rate with exponents between 0.54 and 0.64, even for low scan rates at which the charge flow is close to the Li intercalation capacity.  Also, the authors have tested a method proposed in the literature for differentiating between faradaic and pseudocapacitive charge storage from scan rate-dependent cyclic voltammograms.  The obtained results are not phys. meaningful, in particular the obtained neg. pseudocapacitive and faradaic currents.  The authors analyzed the origin of these results, and iso-potential plots of the scan rate-dependent current are not suitable for differentiating between faradaic and pseudocapacitive processes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-ePl3cDLI7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7daaC72bxUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlsVOmtbY%253D&amp;md5=3ed9ea605fedc9e6a13a44e2e736f040</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201802200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Malyi, O.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Selective Ionic Transport Pathways in Phosphorene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nie, Anmin; Cheng, Yingchun; Ning, Shoucong; Foroozan, Tara; Yasaei, Poya; Li, Wen; Song, Boao; Yuan, Yifei; Chen, Lin; Salehi-Khojin, Amin; Mashayek, Farzad; Shahbazian-Yassar, Reza</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2240-2247</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
