            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite many theor. predictions indicating exceptionally low energy barriers of ionic transport in phosphorene, the ionic transport pathways in this two-dimensional (2D) material was not exptl. demonstrated.  Here, using in situ aberration-cor. TEM and d. functional theory, the authors studied sodium ion transport in phosphorene.  The authors' high-resoln. TEM imaging complemented by EELS demonstrates a precise description of anisotropic sodium ions migration along the [100] direction in phosphorene.  This work also provides new insight into the effect of surface and the edge sites on the transport properties of phosphorene.  According to the authors' observation, the sodium ion transport is preferred in zigzag edge rather than the armchair edge.  The use of this highly selective ionic transport property may endow phosphorene with new functionalities for novel chem. device applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpgi00RN-M4xrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7daaC72bxUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xkt1Cnu7Y%253D&amp;md5=ba96606103ffacee95699608ae63ae51</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C8MH00156A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitance Contribution in Boron-Doped Graphite Sheets for Anion Storage Enables High-Performance Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Mater. Horiz.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">535</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8MH00156A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D529-535%26journal%3DMater.%2BHoriz.%26author%3DF.%2BYu%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DR.%2BZhou%26author%3DD.%2BTan%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BWang%26title%3DPseudocapacitance%2BContribution%2Bin%2BBoron-Doped%2BGraphite%2BSheets%2Bfor%2BAnion%2BStorage%2BEnables%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BCapacitors%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8MH00156A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c14611&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8MH00156A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitance contribution in boron-doped graphite sheets for anion storage enables high-performance sodium-ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Feng; Liu, Zaichun; Zhou, Renwu; Tan, Deming; Wang, Hongxia; Wang, Faxing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Horizons</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">529-535</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MHAOBM</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2051-6355</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on metal-ion hybrid capacitors is emerging as one of the hottest topics in energy storage fields because of their combination of high power and energy densities.  To improve the sluggish faradaic reaction in traditional electrode materials for metal-ion hybrid capacitors, intercalation pseudocapacitive materials have been developed as attractive candidates.  However, all the previously reported pseudocapacitances in intercalation/deintercalation reactions are based on cations (Li+, Na+, Zn2+etc.).  In this work, we demonstrated the high pseudocapacitance contribution in boron-doped graphite (BG) sheets by taking advantage of anion storage.  The BG electrode can reversibly store anions (PF6-) through both a surface-controlled pseudocapacitive reaction and a diffusion-limited intercalation/deintercalation reaction.  The fabricated Na-ion hybrid capacitor with a BG cathode exhibits superior electrochem. performance.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High-Voltage, Dendrite-Free, and Durable Zn-Graphite Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Gang; Kohn, Benjamin; Scheler, Ulrich; Wang, Faxing; Oswald, Steffen; Loeffler, Markus; Tan, Deming; Zhang, Panpan; Zhang, Jian; Feng, Xinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intrinsic advantages of metallic Zn, like high theor. capacity (820 mAh g-1), high abundance, low toxicity, and high safety have driven the recent booming development of rechargeable Zn batteries.  However, the lack of high-voltage electrolyte and cathode materials restricts the cell voltage mostly to below 2 V.  Moreover, dendrite formation and the poor rechargeability of the Zn anode hinder the long-term operation of Zn batteries.  Here a high-voltage and durable Zn-graphite battery, which is enabled by a LiPF6-contg. hybrid electrolyte, is reported.  The presence of LiPF6 efficiently suppresses the anodic oxidn. of Zn electrolyte and leads to a super-wide electrochem. stability window of 4 V (vs Zn/Zn2+).  Both dendrite-free Zn plating/stripping and reversible dual-anion intercalation into the graphite cathode are realized in the hybrid electrolyte.  The resultant Zn-graphite battery performs stably at a high voltage of 2.8 V with a record midpoint discharge voltage of 2.2 V.  After 2000 cycles at a high charge-discharge rate, high capacity retention of 97.5% is achieved with ≈100% Coulombic efficiency.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq09_TVtSp9bbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7daaC72bxUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit12isLzK&amp;md5=3905e46a6b515d6d52ab56e405893674</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104594"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sari, H.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlled design of metal oxide-based (Mn2+/Nb5+) anodes for superior sodium-ion hybrid supercapacitors: Synergistic mechanisms of hybrid ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Jian; Sari, Hirbod Maleki Kheimeh; Wang, Xiujuan; Yang, Huijuan; Zhang, Jiujun; Li, Xifei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">71</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, metal oxides (Mn2+/Nb5+) embedded into interconnected hollow carbon nanoboxes (MnO@HCNb and NaNbO3@HCNb) are fabricated by a simple template-assisted CVD method.  Such a unique structure provides shortened solid-state transportation pathway and sufficient adsorption sites for Na+, with differing energy storage mechanisms from traditional Faradic reaction.  Benefiting from it, the MnO@HCNb electrode exhibits an outstanding rate performance and an ultra-long lifespan of more than 10,000 cycles with 88.6% of capacity retention, which is rarely reported for oxide-based anodes.  Moreover, energy storage mechanism of the composite and the important role of Mn/Na2O interface generated inside the core (MnO) - shell (C) structure during conversion reaction have been revealed.  Hybrid ion storage mechanisms (adsorption, Faradic reaction and intercalation) are proposed with desirable compatibility, exhibiting uniform capacitive electrochem. behavior.  Coupling with activated carbon cathode, a full cell of Na-HSC demonstrates a high energy d. of 116 Wh kg-1 at 99 W kg-1 and 56.4 Wh kg-1 at 1.8 kW kg-1.  Indeed, this work is inspiring to other researchers to further improve the electrochem. performance of anode materials by adjusting their energy storage mechanisms through structural reconstruction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh1cwLpHK72rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7daaC72bxUQ"> &gt;&gt;             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion capacitors (SICs) have attracted growing attentions since they can combine advantages of Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and electrochem. capacitors simultaneously.  The key point of constructing SICs focuses on developing high electron conductive anode materials and overcome huge vol. variation during sodiation/desodiation process to improve excellent cycling stability and rate performance.  Here, lamellar Mo2C nanosheets assembled by Mo2C nanoparticles (NPs) were synthesized via a facile hydrolysis method with a calcination process, demonstrating an outstanding rate capability with superior cycle stability at 0.5 A/g after 1200 cycles (0.097% decay per cycle from the 2nd to the 1200th cycle) in half cell.  After coupling with com. activated C cathode, SICs demonstrates a high energy and power d. of 76.1 Wh/Kg at 112 W/Kg and an excellent cycle life with 83% of the capacity retained after 4000 cycles.  The research presents that the lamellar Mo2C nanosheets assembled by Mo2C nanoparticles as a competitive anode material for sodium ion hybrid devices can accommodate the vol. change during the sodiation/desodiation and shorten the Na+ diffusion path because of its interconnected lamellar structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVS5C5mcLJhbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSuDS8oWW0BQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Identifying the origin and contribution of pseudocapacitive sodium ion storage in tungsten disulphide nanosheets for application in sodium-ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Chunxia; Huang, Ting; Tao, Yaping; Tan, Deming; Zhang, Yin; Wang, Faxing; Yu, Feng; Xie, Qingji</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na)-ion capacitors are emerging as one of the most promising hybrid devices for next generation electrochem. energy storage systems because of their abundant resources, and environmentally friendly nature as well as the potential integration of Na-ion batteries with high energy d. and electrochem. capacitors with high power d.  However, the practical application of Na-ion capacitors is severely hampered by the sluggish redox kinetics in anodes.  To overcome this obstacle, the most effective approach is to develop a pseudocapacitive anode material for Na ion storage.  Here, we demonstrate a predominant pseudocapacitive contribution for Na ion storage in tungsten disulfide (WS2) nanosheets within the potential window of 1-3 V vs. Na/Na+.  Particularly, the root cause of pseudocapacitive Na ion storage in WS2 nanosheets was systematically investigated by operando X-ray diffraction (XRD), ex situ synchronous radiation tests and d. functional theory (DFT) simulations.  This work may provide a fundamental insight into the development of pseudocapacitive materials for electrochem. energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpGQzNc4Lm3c7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSuDS8oWW0BQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVKksrjO&amp;md5=34ec8ee90eaa155172628bc884184385</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202008318"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y. N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Yolk-Shell-Structured FePO<sub>4</sub>Cathode for High-Rate and Long-Cycling Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>59</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17504</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17510</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202008318</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D59%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D17504-17510%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BDu%26author%3DQ.%2BC.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BN.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BBao%26author%3DJ.%2BShen%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26title%3DA%2BYolk-Shell-Structured%2BFePO4Cathode%2Bfor%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BLong-Cycling%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.202008318&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c14611&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.202008318&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Yolk-Shell-Structured FePO4 Cathode for High-Rate and Long-Cycling Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhuangzhuang; Du, Yichen; Wang, Qin-Chao; Xu, Jingyi; Zhou, Yong-Ning; Bao, Jianchun; Shen, Jian; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17504-17510</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous iron phosphate (FePO4) has attracted enormous attention as a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. specific capacity and superior electrochem. reversibility.  Nevertheless, the low rate performance and rapid capacity decline seriously hamper its implementation in SIBs.  Herein, we demonstrate a sagacious multi-step templating approach to skillfully craft amorphous FePO4 yolk-shell nanospheres with mesoporous nanoyolks supported inside the robust porous outer nanoshells.  Their unique architecture and large surface area enable these amorphous FePO4 yolk-shell nanospheres to manifest remarkable sodium storage properties with high reversible capacity, outstanding rate performance, and ultralong cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq13OS6MCvasrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSuDS8oWW0BQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFyhtrzF&amp;md5=cf3e684439234eac63ad3a0e9fd0bc00</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201908918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enabling Superior Electrochemical Properties for Highly Efficient Potassium Storage by Impregnating Ultrafine Sb Nanocrystals within Nanochannel-Containing Carbon Nanofibers</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>58</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14578</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14583</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.201908918</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D58%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D14578-14583%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26author%3DX.%2BGe%26author%3DS.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BQiao%26author%3DY.%2BDu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BBao%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26title%3DEnabling%2BSuperior%2BElectrochemical%2BProperties%2Bfor%2BHighly%2BEfficient%2BPotassium%2BStorage%2Bby%2BImpregnating%2BUltrafine%2BSb%2BNanocrystals%2Bwithin%2BNanochannel-Containing%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.201908918&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c14611&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201908918&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enabling Superior Electrochemical Properties for Highly Efficient Potassium Storage by Impregnating Ultrafine Sb Nanocrystals within Nanochannel-Containing Carbon Nanofibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xufang; Liu, Shuhu; Qiao, Man; Du, Yichen; Li, Yafei; Bao, Jianchun; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14578-14583</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-based nanocomposites are attractive anode materials for batteries as they exhibit large theor. capacity and impressive working voltage.  However, tardy potassium ion diffusion characteristics, unstable Sb/electrolyte interphase, and huge vol. variation pose a challenge, hindering their practical use for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  Now, a simple robust strategy is presented for uniformly impregnating ultrasmall Sb nanocrystals within carbon nanofibers contg. an array of hollow nanochannels (denoted u-Sb@CNFs), resolving the issues above and yielding high-performance PIBs. u-Sb@CNFs can be directly employed as an anode, thereby dispensing with the need for conductive additives and binders.  Such a judiciously crafted u-Sb@CNF-based anode renders a set of intriguing electrochem. properties, representing large charge capacity, unprecedented cycling stability, and outstanding rate performance.  A reversible capacity of 225 mAh g-1 is retained after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpu8PuXcfUuw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSuDS8oWW0BQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhslWkurfI&amp;md5=95d6b34a5b6fb653ce971b53ee0a03fd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.03.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, X.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Feasible Engineering of Cathode Electrolyte Interphase enables the Profoundly Improved Electrochemical Properties in Dual-Ion Battery</span>. <i>J. Energy Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>50</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">416</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">423</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jechem.2020.03.043</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D50%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D416-423%26journal%3DJ.%2BEnergy%2BChem.%26author%3DW.-H.%2BLi%26author%3DH.-J.%2BLiang%26author%3DX.-K.%2BHou%26author%3DZ.-Y.%2BGu%26author%3DX.-X.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.-Z.%2BGuo%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DX.-L.%2BWu%26title%3DFeasible%2BEngineering%2Bof%2BCathode%2BElectrolyte%2BInterphase%2Benables%2Bthe%2BProfoundly%2BImproved%2BElectrochemical%2BProperties%2Bin%2BDual-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jechem.2020.03.043&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c14611&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jechem.2020.03.043&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">167</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">173</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat5029</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemrev.8b00116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paek, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Review of Hybrid Ion Capacitors: from Aqueous to Lithium to Sodium</span>. <i>Chem. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>118</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6457</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6498</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemrev.8b00116</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review of Hybrid Ion Capacitors: From Aqueous to Lithium to Sodium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Jia; Hu, Wenbin; Paek, Eunsu; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">118</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6457-6498</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this crit. Review we focus on the evolution of the hybrid ion capacitor (HIC) from its early embodiments to its modern form, focusing on the key outstanding scientific and technol. questions that necessitate further in-depth study.  It may be argued that HICs began as aq. systems, based on a Faradaic oxide pos. electrode (e.g., Co3O4, RuOx) and an activated carbon ion-adsorption neg. electrode.  In these early embodiments HICs were meant to compete directly with elec. double layer capacitors (EDLCs), rather than with the much higher energy secondary batteries.  The HIC design then evolved to be based on a wide voltage (∼4.2 V) carbonate-based battery electrolyte, using an insertion titanium oxide compd. anode (Li4Ti5O12, LixTi5O12) vs. a Li ion adsorption porous carbon cathode.  The modern Na and Li architectures contain a diverse range of nanostructured materials in both electrodes, including TiO2, Li7Ti5O12, Li4Ti5O12, Na6LiTi5O12, Na2Ti3O7, graphene, hard carbon, soft carbon, graphite, carbon nanosheets, pseudocapacitor T-Nb2O5, V2O5, MXene, conversion compds. MoS2, VN, MnO, and Fe2O3/Fe3O4, cathodes based on Na3V2(PO4)3, NaTi2(PO4)3, sodium super ionic conductor (NASICON), etc.  The Ragone chart characteristics of HIC devices critically depend on their anode-cathode architectures.  Combining electrodes with the flattest capacity vs. voltage characteristics, and the largest total voltage window, yields superior energy.  Unfortunately "flat voltage" materials undergo significant vol. expansion/contraction during cycling and are frequently lifetime limited.  Overall more research on HIC cathodes is needed; apart from high surface area carbon, very few pos. electrodes demonstrate the necessary 10 000 or 100 000 plus cycle life.  It remains to be detd. whether its lithium ion capacitors (LICs) or sodium ion capacitors (NICs) are superior in terms of energy-power and cyclability.  We discuss unresolved issues, including poorly understood fast-charge storage mechanisms, prelithiation and presodiation, solid electrolyte interface (SEI) formation, and high-rate metal plating.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrewdRK0N8NObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-jFe0-8H58Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1Sqtb7P&amp;md5=7d4cc9accdc9edb9cb6ec78504bf3620</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE02070D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Positive Electrode Materials for Post-Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Nanotechnol. has opened up new frontiers in materials science and engineering in the past several decades.  Considerable efforts on nanostructured electrode materials have been made in recent years to fulfill the future requirements of electrochem. energy storage.  Compared to bulk materials, most of these nanostructured electrode materials improve the thermodn. and kinetic properties of electrochem. reactions for achieving high energy and power densities.  Here we briefly review the state-of-the-art research activities in the area of nanostructured pos. electrode materials for post-lithium ion batteries, including Li-S batteries, Li-Se batteries, aq. rechargeable lithium batteries, Li-O2 batteries, Na-ion batteries, Mg-ion batteries and Al-ion batteries.  These future rechargeable battery systems may offer increased energy densities, reduced cost, and more environmental benignity.  A particular focus is directed to the design principles of these nanostructured pos. electrode materials and how nanostructuring influences electrochem. performance.  Moreover, the recent achievements in nanostructured pos. electrode materials for some of the latest emerging rechargeable batteries are also summarized, such as Zn-ion batteries, F- and Cl-ion batteries, Na-, K- and Al-S batteries, Na- and K-O2 batteries, Li-CO2 batteries, novel Zn-air batteries, and hybrid redox flow batteries.  To facilitate further research and development, some future research trends and directions are finally discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9_eyoH8Ij6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-jFe0-8H58Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFKjtr3E&amp;md5=4875475022bc8842c68bc83b761e177c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201800028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cuniberti, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Dual-Stimuli-Responsive Sodium-Bromine Battery with Ultrahigh Energy Density</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although sodium hybrid capacitors (NHCs) have emerged as one of the most promising next-generation energy storage systems, further advancement is delayed primarily by the absence of high-performance battery-type anodes.  Herein, we report a nature-inspired synthesis route to prep. hard carbon anodes with high capacity, rate capability, and cycle stability for dual-carbon NHCs.  Shape- and size-controllable crystal aggregates of inexpensive triazine mols. are utilized as reactive templates that perform triple duties of structure-directing agent, porogen, and nitrogen source.  This enables the fine control of microstructure/morphol./compn. and thereby electrochem. reactions toward Na-ion.  The resulting hard carbon optimized in terms of lateral size, interlayer spacing, and surface affinity of graphene-like layers achieves a specific capacity of ∼380 mAh/g after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 250 mA/g mainly via intercalation, the current record of hard carbons.  Combined with a com. microporous carbon fiber cathode, the full cell is able to deliver a volumetric energy d. of 2.89 mWh/cm3 and a volumetric power d. of 160 mW/cm3, outperforming NHCs based on inorg. Na-ion anode materials.  More importantly, such performance could not only be retained for 10000 cycles (4.5 F/cm3 at 10 mA/cm3) with 0.000 028 6% loss per cycle at &gt;97% Coulombic efficiency but also successfully transferred to flexible pouch cells without significant performance loss after 300 bending cycles or during wrapping at a 10R condition.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing electrochem. energy storage devices with high energy-power densities, long cycling life, as well as low cost is of great significance.  Sodium-ion capacitors (NICs), with Na+ as carriers, are composed of a high capacity battery-type electrode and a high rate capacitive electrode.  However, unlike their lithium-ion analogs, the research on NICs is still in its infancy.  Rational material designs still need to be developed to meet the increasing requirements for NICs with superior energy-power performance and low cost.  In the past few years, various materials have been explored to develop NICs with the merits of superior electrochem. performance, low cost, good stability, and environmental friendliness.  Here, the material design strategies for sodium-ion capacitors are summarized, with focus on cathode materials, anode materials, and electrolytes.  The challenges and opportunities ahead for the future research on materials for NICs are also proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDLk9bvcz3w7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-jFe0-8H58Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVCmsLfM&amp;md5=7be1522fec67c8ece2880323bb2a21b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201802272"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paek, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Direct Structure-Performance Comparison of All-Carbon Potassium and Sodium Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/advs.201802272</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct Structure-Performance Comparison of All-Carbon Potassium and Sodium Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Ziqiang; Wu Mengqiang; Chen Zhi; Chen Cheng; Yang Jian; Feng Tingting; Paek Eunsu; Mitlin David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A hybrid ion capacitor (HIC) based on potassium ions (K(+)) is a new high-power intermediate energy device that may occupy a unique position on the Ragone chart space.  Here, a direct performance comparison of a potassium ion capacitor (KIC) versus the better-known sodium ion capacitor is provided.  Tests are performed with an asymmetric architecture based on bulk ion insertion, partially ordered, dense carbon anode (hard carbon, HC) opposing N- and O-rich ion adsorption, high surface area, cathode (activated carbon, AC).  A classical symmetric "supercapacitor-like" configuration AC-AC is analyzed in parallel.  For asymmetric K-based HC-AC devices, there are significant high-rate limitations associated with ion insertion into the anode, making it much inferior to Na-based HC-AC devices.  A much larger charge-discharge hysteresis (overpotential), more than an order of magnitude higher impedance RSEI, and much worse cyclability are observed.  However, K-based AC-AC devices obtained on-par energy, power, and cyclability with their Na counterpart.  Therefore, while KICs are extremely scientifically interesting, more work is needed to tailor the structure of  "Na-inherited" dense carbon anodes and electrolytes for satisfactory K ion insertion.  Conversely, it should be possible to utilize many existing high surface area adsorption carbons for fast rate K application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGccaQRmYaT1Zoq0fPSOTvfW6udTcc2eb_vMgqKIoMSbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3MvkslGguw%253D%253D&amp;md5=3f6dbd19dcbb49876486c776bec9f73a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201903895"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Au, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tebyetekerwa, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">All-Cellulose-Based Quasi-Solid-State Sodium-Ion Hybrid Capacitors Enabled by Structural Hierarchy</span>. <i>Adv.     </div><div class="casAbstract">3D printing technology has stimulated a burgeoning interest to fabricate customized architectures in a facile and scalable manner targeting wide ranged energy storage applications.  Nevertheless, 3D-printed hybrid capacitor devices synergizing favorable energy/power density have not yet been explored thus far.  Herein, we demonstrate a 3D-printed sodium-ion hybrid capacitor (SIC) based on nitrogen-doped MXene (N-Ti3C2Tx) anode and activated carbon cathode.  N-Ti3C2Tx affording a well-defined porous structure and uniform nitrogen doping can be obtained via a sacrificial template method.  Thus-formulated ink can be directly printed to form electrode architecture without the request of a conventional current collector.  The 3D-printed SICs, with a large areal mass loading up to 15.2 mg cm(-2), can harvest an areal energy/power density of 1.18 mWh cm(-2)/40.15 mW cm(-2), outperforming the state-of-the-art 3D-printed energy storage devices.         </div><div class="casAbstract">With the relentless development of smart and miniaturized electronics, the worldwide thirst for microscale electrochem. energy storage devices with form factors is launching a new era of competition.  Herein, the first prototype planar sodium-ion microcapacitors are constructed based on the interdigital microelectrodes of urchin-like sodium titanate as faradaic anode and nanoporous activated graphene as non-faradaic cathode along with high-voltage ionogel electrolyte on a single flexible substrate.  By effectively coupling with battery-type anode and capacitor-type cathode, the resultant all-solid-state NIMCs working at 3.5 V exhibit a high volumetric energy d. of 37.1 mWh cm-3 and an ultralow self-discharge rate of 44 h from Vmax to 0.6 Vmax, both of which surpass most reported hybrid micro-supercapacitors.  Through tuning graphene layer covered on the top surface of interdigital microelectrodes, the NIMCs unveil remarkably enhanced power d., owing to the establishment of favorable multidirectional fast ion diffusion pathways that significantly reduce the charge transfer resistance.  Meanwhile, the as-fabricated NIMCs present excellent mech. flexibility without capacitance fade under repeated deformation, and electrochem. stability at a high temp. of 80 °C because of using nonflammable ionogel electrolyte and in-plane geometry.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLytkg5c6aP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk-yn6gDdDMg"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous nitrogen-doped carbon/carbon nanocomposite electrodes enable sodium ion capacitors with high capacity and rate capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Runyu; Leus, Karen; Hofmann, Jan P.; Antonietti, Markus; Oschatz, Martin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The realization of electrochem. energy storage devices combining high energy and power d. places high demands on the electrode materials.  It remains difficult to provide high metal storage capacity and rate capability at the same time in one and the same material.  By decoupling metal storage and electron transport in different phases of a nanostructured electrode composed of nitrogen-rich carbon nanoparticles which are embedded into a conductive mesoporous carbon matrix, this dilemma can be minimized.  The composite material has a remarkable performance for sodium storage with a reversible capacity of 343 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and capacity retention of 124 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1. At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion battery is a potential sustainable energy storage system due to its abundance and low cost.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6DtWp0JiFJg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-10551-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Co-intercalation reactions make graphite as promising anodes for sodium ion batteries, however, the high redox potentials significantly lower the energy density.  Herein, we investigate the factors that influence the co-intercalation potential of graphite and find that the tuning of the voltage as large as 0.38 V is achievable by adjusting the relative stability of ternary graphite intercalation compounds and the solvent activity in electrolytes.  The feasibility of graphite anode in sodium ion batteries is confirmed in conjunction with Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathodes by using the optimal electrolyte.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The reversible intercalation of solvated Na-ions into graphite and the concomitant formation of ternary Na-graphite intercalation compds. (GICs) are studied using several in operando techniques, such as X-ray-diffraction (XRD), electrochem. scanning tunnelling microscopy (EC-STM) and electrochem. quartz crystal microbalance techniques (EQCM).  Linear ethylene glycol di-Me ether homologues ("glymes") Gx with x + 1 O-atoms were used as solvents, where x is 1-4.  The intercalation mechanism of Na+(Gx)y-complexes was investigated with a focus on the phase transitions and diffusion rates of the Na+(Gx)y-complexes inside the graphite lattice.  For the four shortest glymes (G1 to G4), it is found using XRD that an intermediate stage 2 Na-GIC (NaC48) is formed upon the partial sodiation of the graphite electrode.  At full sodiation stage 1 Na-GIC (NaC18, 112 mA h g-1) is obtained for G1, G2 and G4, while the G3 system also forms a stage 1 Na-GIC but with less Na incorporated (NaC30, 70 mA h g-1).  The phase transitions of a battery electrode upon ion-intercalation are visualised using STM on the at. scale for the first time.  In addn., the local diffusion rates of the intercalated species inside the electrode were detd., a unique approach for detg. kinetic effects in batteries on the at. scale.  The formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is obsd. with STM as well as with an EQCM, while the latter technique is used for novel in situ hydrodynamic spectroscopy, giving further insight into the intercalation mechanism.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpHio6VJZG8HLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6DtWp0JiFJg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The graphite material from exhausted Li-ion batteries (LIBs) is reused as a favorable anode for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) and K-ion batteries (KIBs) through a recycling treatment.                         rightTab-cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of excellent rate and cycle performance of Na+-solvent cointercalated graphite vs. poor performance of Li+-solvent case</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Sung Chul; Kang, Yong-Ju; Han, Young-Kyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite its high reversibility for Li+ intercalation, graphite is known to be electrochem. inactive for Na+ intercalation.  On the contrary, recent studies have demonstrated that graphite is active and shows excellent rate and cycle performance for Na+-solvent cointercalation but it exhibits poor performance for Li+-solvent cointercalation.  Herein, we elucidate the mechanism of Li+- and Na+-solvent cointercalation into graphite and the origin of the strikingly different electrochem. performance of Li+- and Na+-solvent cointercalation cells.  Na+ intercalation into graphite is thermodynamically unfavorable, but Na+-diglyme cointercalation is very favorable.  The diglyme-graphene van der Waals interaction reinforces the interlayer coupling strength and thereby improves the resistance of graphite to exfoliation.  The transport of solvated Na ions is so fast that the diffusivity of Na+-diglyme complexes is markedly faster (by five orders of magnitude) than that of Li+-diglyme complexes.  The very fast Na+-diglyme cond. is attributed to facile sliding of flat diglyme mols., which completely solvate Na ions in the interlayer space of graphite.  The slow Li+-diglyme cond. is ascribed to steric hindrance to codiffusion caused by bent diglyme mols. that incompletely solvate Li ions.  The bent and flat diglyme mols. surrounding Li and Na ions, resp., are highly assocd. with the strong Li+-graphene and weak Na+-graphene interactions, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIBciXioUE5LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHr7xu_Hal0g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktFygtbo%253D&amp;md5=9b106c4199d530c12545837c216bc169</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201801361"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ethers Illume Sodium-Based Battery Chemistry: Uniqueness, Surprise, and Challenges</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHr7xu_Hal0g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2mtbnN&amp;md5=be5958dc01f38deeacf6a2a0eb32101f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acscentsci.5b00328"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seh, Z.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to its low cost and high natural abundance, sodium metal is among the most promising anode materials for energy storage technologies beyond lithium ion batteries.  However, room-temp. sodium metal anodes suffer from poor reversibility during long-term plating and stripping, mainly due to formation of nonuniform solid electrolyte interphase as well as dendritic growth of sodium metal.  Herein it is reported for the first time that a simple liq. electrolyte, sodium hexafluorophosphate in glymes (mono-, di-, and tetraglyme), can enable highly reversible and nondendritic plating-stripping of sodium metal anodes at room temp.  High av. Coulombic efficiencies of 99.9% were achieved over 300 plating-stripping cycles at 0.5 mA cm-2.  The long-term reversibility was found to arise from the formation of a uniform, inorg. solid electrolyte interphase made of sodium oxide and sodium fluoride, which is highly impermeable to electrolyte solvent and conducive to nondendritic growth.  As a proof of concept, a room-temp. sodium-sulfur battery is demonstrated using this class of electrolytes, paving the way for the development of next-generation, sodium-based energy storage technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdqXOWzEW74bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHr7xu_Hal0g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVGmtrfL&amp;md5=6155e3c781a24b8340081c2ad4444616</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1021/ja5017156"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parvez, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z. Here the authors report a prompt electrochem. exfoliation of graphene sheets into aq. solns. of different inorg. salts ((NH4)2SO4, Na2SO4, K2SO4, etc.).  Exfoliation in these electrolytes leads to graphene with a high yield (&gt;85%, ≤3 layers), large lateral size (up to 44 μm), low oxidn. degree (a C/O ratio of 17.2), and a remarkable hole mobility of 310 cm2 V-1 s-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The insertion of guest species in graphite is the key feature utilized in applications ranging from energy storage and liq. purifn. to the synthesis of graphene.  Recently, it was discovered that solvated-Na-ion intercalation can occur in graphite even though the insertion of Na ions alone is thermodynamically impossible; this phenomenon enables graphite to function as a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.  In an effort to understand this unusual behavior, we investigate the solvated-Na-ion intercalation mechanism using in operando X-ray diffraction anal., electrochem. titrn., real-time optical observation, and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns.  The ultrafast intercalation is demonstrated in real time using millimeter-sized highly ordered pyrolytic graphite, in which instantaneous insertion of solvated-Na-ions occurs (in less than 2 s).  The formation of various stagings with solvated-Na-ions in graphite is obsd. and precisely quantified for the first time.  The atomistic configuration of the solvated-Na-ions in graphite is proposed based on the exptl. results and DFT calcns.  The correlation between the properties of various solvents and the Na ion co-intercalation further suggests a strategy to tune the electrochem. performance of graphite electrodes in Na rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphq0hB-9yin7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6ZhwIbvQVsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlaqurzN&amp;md5=250c7333d104659b257c418527d2f55e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1038/nmat4810"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cook, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The short charging times and high power capabilities assocd. with capacitive energy storage make this approach an attractive alternative to batteries.  One limitation of electrochem. capacitors is their low energy d. and for this reason, there is widespread interest in pseudocapacitive materials that use Faradaic reactions to store charge.  One candidate pseudocapacitive material is orthorhombic MoO3 (α-MoO3), a layered compd. with a high theor. capacity for lithium (279 mA h g-1 or 1,005 C g-1).  Here, we report on the properties of reduced α-MoO3-x(R-MoO3-x) and compare it with fully oxidized α-MoO3 (F-MoO3).  The introduction of oxygen vacancies leads to a larger interlayer spacing that promotes faster charge storage kinetics and enables the α-MoO3 structure to be retained during the insertion and removal of Li ions.  The higher specific capacity of the R-MoO3-x is attributed to the reversible formation of a significant amt. of Mo4+ following lithiation.  This study underscores the potential importance of incorporating oxygen vacancies into transition metal oxides as a strategy for increasing the charge storage kinetics of redox-active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9QgRHEtnVrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6ZhwIbvQVsA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-iodine (Na-I2) batteries are attracting growing attention for grid-scale energy storage due to their abundant resources, low cost, environmental friendliness, high theor. capacity (211 mAh g-1), and excellent electrochem. reversibility.  Nevertheless, the practical application of Na-I2 batteries is severely hindered by their poor cycle stability owing to the serious dissoln. of polyiodide in the electrolyte during charge/discharge processes.  Herein, the at. modulation of metal-bis(dihydroxy) species in a fully conjugated phthalocyanine copper metal-org. framework (MOF) for suppression of polyiodide dissoln. toward long-time cycling Na-I2 batteries is demonstrated.  The Fe2[(2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxy phthalocyaninato)Cu] MOF composited with I2 (Fe2-O8-PcCu/I2) serves as a cathode for a Na-I2 battery exhibiting a stable specific capacity of 150 mAh g-1 after 3200 cycles and outperforming the state-of-the-art cathodes for Na-I2 batteries.  Operando spectroelectrochem. and electrochem. kinetics analyses together with d. functional theory calcns. reveal that the square planar iron-bis(dihydroxy) (Fe-O4) species in Fe2-O8-PcCu are responsible for the binding of polyiodide to restrain its dissoln. into electrolyte.  Besides the monovalent Na-I2 batteries in org. electrolytes, the Fe2-O8-PcCu/I2 cathode also operates stably in other metal-I2 batteries like aq. multivalent Zn-I2 batteries.  Thus, this work offers a new strategy for designing stable cathode materials toward high-performance metal-iodine batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhvcsvJGd9v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6ZhwIbvQVsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlGhsbzO&amp;md5=0d741d425306ce9906ec6dd05d3b31fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202000287"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tseng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Stimulus-Responsive Zinc-Iodine Battery with Smart Overcharge Self-Protection Function</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Zinc-iodine aq. batteries (ZIABs) are highly attractive for grid-scale energy storage due to their high theor. capacities, environmental friendliness, and intrinsic non-flammability.  However, because of the close redox potential of Zn stripping/platting and hydrogen evolution, slight overcharge of ZIABs would induce drastic side reactions, serious safety concerns, and battery failure.  A novel type of stimulus-responsive zinc-iodine aq. battery (SR-ZIAB) with fast overcharge self-protection ability is demonstrated by employing a smart pH-responsive electrolyte.  Operando spectroelectrochem. characterizations reveal that the battery failure mechanism of ZIABs during overcharge arises from the increase of electrolyte pH induced by hydrogen evolution as well as the consequent irreversible formation of insulating ZnO at anode and sol. Zn(IO3)2 at cathode.  Under overcharge conditions, the designed SR-ZIABs can be rapidly switched off with capacity degrading to 6% of the initial capacity, thereby avoiding continuous battery damage.  Importantly, SR-ZIABs can be switched on with nearly 100% of capacity recovery by re-adjusting the electrolyte pH.  This work will inspire the development of aq. Zn batteries with smart self-protection ability in the overcharge state.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmkDQhzRAHrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6ZhwIbvQVsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXksVKjsbc%253D&amp;md5=420bb5825ba13bcc6777faf3ae76eb57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.07.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, F.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design and Synthesis of Electrode Materials with Both Battery-Type and Capacitive Charge Storage</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">235</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">255</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">There is a growing need for energy storage devices in numerous applications where a large amt. of energy needs to be either stored or delivered quickly.  The present paper details the study of alkali-ion intercalation pseudo-capacitance in ultrathin VOPO4 nanosheets, which hold promise in high-rate alkali-ion based electrochem. energy storage.  Starting from bulk VOPO4·2H2O chunks, VOPO4 nanosheets were obtained through simple ultrasonication in isoPrOH.  These nanosheets as the cathode exhibit a specific capacity of 154 and 136 mA h/g (close to theor. value 166 mA h/g) for Li and Na storage devices at 0.1 C and 100 and ∼70 mA h/g at 5 C, demonstrating their high rate capability.  Also, the capacity retention is maintained at 90% for Li ion storage and 73% for Na ion storage after 500 cycles, showing their reasonable stability.  The demonstrated alkali-ion intercalation pseudo-capacitance represents a promising direction for developing battery materials with promising high rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcpNKNsHXvp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig1RsXLu4I5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVejtb3F&amp;md5=1da7e7e855bb254dd6f51c674fbb8c11</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.03.186"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Opitz, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wallauer, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Smarsly, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Roling, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanisms of Charge Storage in Nanoparticulate TiO<sub>2</sub> and Li<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>5</sub>O<sub>12</sub> Anodes: New Insights from Scan Rate-Dependent Cyclic Voltammetry</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors have studied Li intercalation into two nanoparticulate anode materials for Li ion batteries, Nb-doped TiO2 (Nb-TiO2) and Li4Ti5O12 (LTO), by scan rate-dependent cyclic voltammetry.  The av. particle size is 7 nm for Nb-TiO2 and 6 nm for LTO, resp.  For both materials, the authors observe a transition in the scan rate dependence of the charge flow, from Li intercalation capacity control at low scan rates to diffusion/phase transformation control at higher scan rates.  The peak current densities exhibit an approx. power law dependence on the scan rate with exponents between 0.54 and 0.64, even for low scan rates at which the charge flow is close to the Li intercalation capacity.  Also, the authors have tested a method proposed in the literature for differentiating between faradaic and pseudocapacitive charge storage from scan rate-dependent cyclic voltammograms.  The obtained results are not phys. meaningful, in particular the obtained neg. pseudocapacitive and faradaic currents.  The authors analyzed the origin of these results, and iso-potential plots of the scan rate-dependent current are not suitable for differentiating between faradaic and pseudocapacitive processes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-ePl3cDLI7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig1RsXLu4I5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlsVOmtbY%253D&amp;md5=3ed9ea605fedc9e6a13a44e2e736f040</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201802200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Malyi, O.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite many theor. predictions indicating exceptionally low energy barriers of ionic transport in phosphorene, the ionic transport pathways in this two-dimensional (2D) material was not exptl. demonstrated.  Here, using in situ aberration-cor. TEM and d. functional theory, the authors studied sodium ion transport in phosphorene.  The authors' high-resoln. TEM imaging complemented by EELS demonstrates a precise description of anisotropic sodium ions migration along the [100] direction in phosphorene.  This work also provides new insight into the effect of surface and the edge sites on the transport properties of phosphorene.  According to the authors' observation, the sodium ion transport is preferred in zigzag edge rather than the armchair edge.  The use of this highly selective ionic transport property may endow phosphorene with new functionalities for novel chem. device applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpgi00RN-M4xrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig1RsXLu4I5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xkt1Cnu7Y%253D&amp;md5=ba96606103ffacee95699608ae63ae51</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C8MH00156A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitance Contribution in Boron-Doped Graphite Sheets for Anion Storage Enables High-Performance Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Mater.
